Three More Kidnappers Apprehended in the Wu Nanpu Case

Wu Zeyun, also known as Nanpu, a broker at the Huashang Cloth Exchange No. 49 from Jiangxi Province, was kidnapped on the 7th of this month and a ransom of 400,000 yuan was demanded. Lu Liankui, the chief inspector of the general inspectorate of the general police station, rescued Wu from the kidnappers' den in a bungalow at the Fangjia Wood Bridge in Beixinjing, and arrested eight kidnappers, including Lu Wen. The report has been published in this newspaper that they were handed over to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Subsequently, another accomplice, Zhang Wenlong, was apprehended in Room 24 of the Suzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road and sent to the Criminal Division 1 of the Special Court the day before yesterday for interrogation by Judge Xu Jiashi. Li Zhishan, the police station's lawyer, stated that Zhang had previously served as a detective in the Chinese area and had now resigned. Zhang confessed that he had been called by the already apprehended suspect Sun Jinpeng to negotiate the ransom and also confessed that he was involved in the kidnapping of Deng Zhonghe, the owner of the Daqing Cloth Store, and had received 160 yuan. However, as this case was being handled by Judge Zhou, he requested a postponement to combine the cases for interrogation. Judge Xu questioned Zhang briefly and ordered a postponement for a combined interrogation. In addition, Chinese Detective Shang Wu of the Huizi Police Station apprehended three more accomplices from Tongzhou, Lu A Hai, Li Wenbin, and Lu Caiwu, at the Meibaike Road and Wuzhen Road Bridge the day before yesterday and sent them to the Criminal Division 1 of the Special Court yesterday morning. The police station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, requested a postponement for a combined interrogation. When Li Wenbin was questioned, he confessed that he was responsible for taking photos in this case (i.e., identifying the plaintiff's common name), and Lu Caiwu confessed that he had rented a house for the bandits to hide the ticket. Judge Zhou verified the confessions and ordered the detention of the three defendants, Lu, and postponed the hearing for a combined interrogation.

Case of Injury to Wang Youling

Zhang Debiao Sentenced to 15 Days of Detention

Lawyer Wang Youling, also known as Zijian, practiced law in Shanghai and set up his office at No. 100 Beijing Road. At 5:20 pm on the 5th of this month, Wang was leaving his office and was about to board his car when suddenly a man from Anhui named Zhang Debiao threw a can full of fecal matter at Wang's face, causing Wang's face to be covered in yellow and white matter, which smelled terrible. Zhang, seeing that his goal had been achieved, fled the scene. Wang's driver chased and apprehended him, and turned him over to the police station. The next morning, he was sent to the First Special Court. Wang Youling presented a doctor's injury certificate, so the police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, prosecuted him for the crime of injury under Article 293 of the Criminal Law. Zhang Debiao claimed that he had repeatedly failed to recover a debt from a certain Han, so he harbored resentment and threw feces at him, but accidentally hit lawyer Wang, which was unintentional, and asked for leniency. The judge verified the confession and ordered Zhang to provide a guarantor to be available at any time, and the case was postponed for further hearing. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Shumu held a further hearing. Zhang Debiao's confession was the same as before. The police station's lawyer Qian requested a heavy sentence. Zhang's lawyer argued that the injury certificate presented by lawyer Wang only stated that his eyes were slightly red and awaited further changes. However, lawyer Wang's face was originally red, so it was difficult to prove whether his eyes were slightly red because of this incident. Moreover, lawyer Wang did not appear in court today and requested that he be declared not guilty. Judge Shen verified the confession and announced the verdict in court, sentencing Zhang Debiao to 15 days of detention as a warning.

Compensation Increased at Slaughterhouse

The Health Director of the Public Works Department suggested revising the compensation regulations for the prohibition of the sale of meat at the slaughterhouse, which has now been approved by the Public Works Department Board of Directors. The price paid by the bureau for dead pigs that are prohibited from sale has been increased from a maximum of five cents per pound to seven cents. The price of dead cattle has been set at four and a half cents per pound. As for livestock that is sold, the skin and carcass are divided into two payments, with the carcass being three cents per pound and the skin being two cents less than the market price per pound.

Yuanlaihang Potato Flour Case

Falsely Claiming to be Eastern Flour, Should Bear All Responsibilities

Fined 40,000 Yuan to be Used for Flood Relief

The Yuanlaihang potato flour case was detained by the former Anti-Japanese and Aid Overseas Chinese Association on August 15 of last year and decided to confiscate it. On October 24, the firm submitted evidence of purchasing from the Netherlands and requested a review. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association then decided to fine 40,000 yuan for flood relief and returned the original goods to the firm. Yesterday, the association specially sent a letter to Yuanlaihang and the fundraising associations of various provinces to investigate and handle the case. The original letter is as follows: Respected Sir, regarding the Yuanlaihang potato flour case, it was previously decided at the ninth executive committee meeting of this association to allocate all the goods to urgent disaster relief donations, and the warehouse receipt was sent to your association for verification and collection. Subsequently, the firm submitted various pieces of evidence and applied for reconsideration. The meeting again decided to review the case and sent a letter to your association to temporarily suspend the disposal of the goods. Now, the 19th executive committee, based on the review report, has repeated its decision as follows: "The goods detained by the Anti-Japanese and Aid Overseas Chinese Association on August 15 were confiscated and allocated to flood relief based on the standards set by the Anti-Japanese Association in the 17th year of the Republic. On October 24, the firm submitted various pieces of evidence and stated its objections. After reviewing the evidence, the staff of this association found that the evidence of purchasing goods from the Netherlands was reliable. However, the firm did not submit sufficient evidence before the decision to confiscate the goods and falsely claimed to be eastern flour to seek high profits. All responsibilities should be borne by the firm. Since the detained goods have been allocated for disaster relief, the firm can donate 40,000 yuan to offset the relief funds to benefit the disaster victims. The original goods should be retrieved from the Relief Committee." The minutes were recorded and a letter was sent to Yuanlaihang.

Jing'an Temple Temple Fair to be Held as Usual This Year

Public Works Department Has Devised a Solution

Shorten Temple Fair Period to Seven Days

The Jing'an Temple in this city is usually held during the temple fair period from the first to the tenth day of the fourth month of the lunar calendar. During these nine days, vendors gather and tourists crowd the area, causing traffic to be blocked. The Public Works Department of the Public Concession has long had the determination to ban it. The temple fair this year is approaching again, and the Public Works Department has repeatedly ordered the abbot of Jing'an Temple to strictly prohibit it. However, due to the difficulty of eliminating customs and the fact that most of the poor vendors rely on this nine-day temple fair to make a living for the year, the abbot of Jing'an Temple went to the Public Works Department three times to ask for a compromise. It is now known that both parties have discussed and resolved to shorten the nine-day temple fair to seven days. As for vendors setting up stalls, they are limited to the sidewalks and must not encroach on the roads to impede traffic. The entrances of shops on both sides must also leave sidewalks for pedestrians.

Worker Beaten by Japanese Police Interrogated by Court Yesterday

Worker Imprisoned for Settling Wages

Since the Japanese-owned yarn factory in Shanghai has been affected by the boycott, many have been unable to maintain operations. At the end of last year, the Tongxing No. 1 Factory at No. 181 Gordon Road dismissed most of its workers, forcibly canceled the usual monthly bonus, and retained only a few workers to carry out the work. The Japanese ordered Japanese policeman No. 54 to beat three workers to the ground, a local worker named Gu Guisong and two workers from Yancheng, Gu Shichang and Chen Deyu. Gu Guisong and Gu Shichang suffered minor head injuries and were discharged from the hospital immediately after being bandaged by the doctor. They were sent to the Simple Court of the First Special Court yesterday. Qian, the police station representative, presented the case and stated that the third defendant, Chen Deyu, was being treated in the hospital due to more serious injuries, and that two Japanese workers had been beaten by the remaining workers and Japanese policeman No. 54 had also been injured and were not present in court, so he requested a postponement. When questioned, the defendants Gu Guisong and Gu Shichang confessed that they had gone to the factory to settle their wages yesterday and were insulted and scolded by the Japanese, and ordered the Japanese police to beat them down with wooden sticks, which angered the workers and caused them to throw stones. Judge Jiang ordered them to be taken back into custody and would investigate after Chen Deyu had recovered.

Rongchangxiang Sues Cheng Linsheng

Judge Orders to Find a Way to Settle

After the tenants failed in the Yixinli Eviction Lawsuit, Rongchangxiang, one of the tenants, had advanced more than 70,000 yuan in construction fees for the landlord, Cheng Linsheng. At that time, the landlord had verbally agreed that after the expiration of the lease, he could renew it for a period of seven years. Therefore, Rongchangxiang hired lawyers Ye Fukan and Yu Hualong to file a counterclaim with the First Special Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren held a hearing. Cheng Linsheng appointed lawyer Liu to appear in court. Judge Zhou said that if the case continued to be litigated, it would be better to settle it, so as to avoid many complications. Therefore, he instructed lawyer Liu to advise Cheng Linsheng to show a slight retreat and consider renewing the lease so that the case could be resolved. Lawyer Liu said that he could accept the court's intention and discuss it with the landlord. Judge Zhou then ordered the case to be postponed for further hearing.

Japanese Exclude Chinese Seafarers

Zhengji Company Also Dismisses Chinese Employees

Dalian Stops Employing Chinese Seafarers: Steamboat sailors and firemen on Japanese merchant ships in Dalian Bay, who have traditionally employed Chinese seafarers, have recently decided, since our country's boycott of Japanese ships, after a meeting by Japanese merchant ships in the port, to dismiss all Chinese sailors and firemen employed on the ships starting this month, and replace them with Japanese. The Dalian Steamship Company is the first to implement this, and replacements are already underway. Other Japanese ships are following suit. It is estimated that at least a thousand Chinese seafarers in Dalian will lose their jobs due to the Japanese exclusion.

Zhengji Employs Japanese: Our country's Zhengji Steamship Company has a great deal of influence in North China. Previously, its shipowners and crew were mostly Japanese. Later, due to the gold standard, Chinese personnel were hired. Recently, however, due to the reduction in the price of gold notes, the company has resumed successively dismissing Chinese crew members and replacing them with Japanese. The other day, the Fuli vessel suddenly dismissed Wang Gongrang, a senior engineer, and forcefully dispatched a Japanese to the ship, causing opposition from the crew. However, General Manager Zhang Zhengben disregarded everything and replaced all senior crew members on all twenty-three ships with Japanese. Currently, more than eighty people have been hired. The dismissed crew members have returned south to Shanghai. Recently, the company has also submitted a request to the Ministry for the issuance of shipowner licenses to Japanese personnel. The Ministry rejected the request. The company submitted a second request, stating that there is a lack of qualified Chinese navigators and that it is necessary to employ Japanese personnel. This matter has not yet been resolved.

After the Labor Unrest in Japanese Textile Factories

Trends in Labor and Management

More than thirty Japanese-owned textile factories in this city, including Rihua and Tongxing (both internal and external), employing more than 60,000 Chinese workers, have been embroiled in a labor strike triggered by opposition to the cancellation of monthly bonuses. Workers from the Xihe factory also joined the strike group yesterday. The details of the situation are as follows:

Japanese Chamber of Commerce Meeting: The Shanghai Japanese Textile Factory Association has not only wired detailed information on the strike to the Osaka Textile Committee for instructions and remedial measures, but has also sent circulars to representatives of all factories in Shanghai, scheduling a representative assembly to seek a fundamental solution. It is said that the upcoming assembly of Japanese textile factories will address three key issues: (1) How to fundamentally resolve the strike triggered by the cancellation of monthly bonuses; (2) If Chinese workers are determined not to return to work until their demands are met, the factory will adopt a firm stance and will not accept any mediation; (3) If the situation becomes deadlocked, the factories will lay off the striking Chinese workers and recruit new workers to replace them. If it is difficult to recruit new workers, they will be recruited from Japan.

Joint Meeting: The Shanghai West Textile Factory Workers' Union held its fourth regular meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss: (1) The case of the Tongxing, Rihua, Xihe, Silk, and other Japanese factories cutting the original monthly bonus and oppressing workers, causing public outrage, and resulting in a strike: It was resolved to provide full assistance; (2) The case of Zhang Xinggui and Fang Xuewen, preparatory committee members of the Huashang Yongyu Textile Factory Workers' Union, being falsely accused by the factory and detained by the Public Security Bureau: It was resolved to report the truth to higher authorities and request assistance from various groups; (3) The case of receiving letters from various universities and anti-Japanese associations inviting participation in the citizens' assembly on the 17th of this month: It was resolved to send representatives to participate; (4) The case of Shi A'si, a female worker in the second cotton mill of the Japanese-owned Internal and External Cotton Mill, being beaten and injured by a Japanese person and then fired: It was resolved to provide assistance. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

General Assembly of Toyo Silk Factory Workers

Seven Demands Put Forward

After the Chinese workers of the first and third factories of the Japanese-owned Toyo Silk Factory in West Shanghai went on strike to protest the cancellation of bonus work by the Japanese, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent staff to mediate yesterday, but the result was unsuccessful due to the tough attitude of the Japanese. All the workers held an inaugural meeting of the labor union at 9:00 AM yesterday in the open space of the Sanguan Temple north of Caojiadu Ham. Representatives from the Shanghai West Cotton Factory Workers' Union, such as Gu Rufang, attended to provide guidance: (1) The chairman was publicly elected to report on the purpose of the meeting; (2) Representatives reported on the Japanese oppression one after another; (3) All matters were discussed; (4) The following resolutions were made: A. Establish the Japanese Silk Factory Workers' Union; B. Elect seventeen executive committee members; C. Elect three standing committee members; D. Determine seven people to be the heads of general affairs, organization, publicity, documents, discipline, communication, and miscellaneous affairs; E. The Shanghai West Cotton Factory Workers' Union will serve as a temporary office from today; F. The names of those elected are not convenient to announce; G. Make the following demands to the factory: (1) The original bonus work must not be deducted; (2) Wages must be paid as usual during the strike; (3) The factory must not dismiss workers without reason; (4) Retirement bonuses should still be paid as before, without deduction; (5) The factory must recognize the union's right to represent workers; (6) Female workers should be paid their full wages for one month during their maternity leave; (7) Double salaries and bonuses at the end of the year. After the record was read aloud to the public, the slogan "We vow not to return to work until our demands are met" was chanted in unison. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Fine of Twenty Yuan

Lu Zongyou from Nanjing recently opened the Xiangong Massage Parlor at No. 277 Xiafei Road in the French Concession without obtaining a license from the Municipal Council to operate privately. When questioned, the defendant admitted to violating the regulations and operating privately without a license. Presiding Judge Wu sentenced the defendant to a fine of twenty yuan as a warning.

The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union convened a joint meeting of the directors of various district branches the other day. Fang Qingjian served as chairman, and formalities were observed. (2) There are no regulations for the period of collection of funds for each district branch. How should this be handled? It was resolved that from now on, it should be collected together with the monthly fees collected by the union. It was resolved that the union's various proposals should be distributed to each district in the future. (4) The union has always stopped working at night. If there is an emergency, it is often impossible to contact. How should this be handled? It was resolved that from now on, the office will be open for two hours every night at the second district branch. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Senlin Rattan, Willow, and Grassware Factory Invents Straw Mattress

The Senlin Rattan, Willow, and Grassware Factory, located across from the Dahua Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in this port, has been open for many years, producing excellent products. The factory manager, Mr. Wu, has extensive experience and insights in this field. Recently, he has collected sedge and yellow grass from various regions and woven straw mats. The colors are bright, and the patterns are exquisite, all with artistic flair. When laid out in various rooms, they are comparable to gauze carpets, but they are inexpensive, durable, and superior in quality. All sizes are available, and there are many items in stock. Buyers are requested to hurry. According to Mr. Wu, this type of straw mat was previously manufactured by Japanese merchants in Shanghai, with annual production exceeding hundreds of thousands of yuan. In order to recover profits and resist Japanese goods, the straw mat department has been greatly expanded and efforts have been made to improve the mats so that Japanese goods will disappear from the market.

Second Branch of the High Court Recruiting Clerks

Jiangsu High Court Second Branch Notice No. 8: Notice for the purpose of announcement. The clerks recruited by the court have been assigned. Now, according to the case law, the approval of the Ministry of Justice has been obtained to hold another examination. It is appropriate to issue a notice in advance in accordance with Article 2 of the Regulations for the Examination and Appointment of Clerks. Registration period: January 25th to 28th. Registration location: the court's receiving and dispatch office. Written test date: January 31st, 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM and 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM. Written test location: this court. Registration fee: one yuan per person, which will not be refunded regardless of whether the exam is taken or passed. Appendix: Articles 4 to 9 of the Regulations for the Examination and Appointment of Clerks. Article 4: Those who take the clerk examination must have the following qualifications: (1) Over 25 years of age; (2) Healthy body; (3) Upright character. Article 5: One of the following situations will disqualify a candidate from taking the exam: (1) Having been sentenced to imprisonment or more, except for state affairs offenders; (2) Having been dismissed from office after disciplinary action; (3) Having a mental illness; (4) Having been a clerk; (5) Having lost property credit. Article 6: To take the clerk examination, a resume and a guarantee of civil servants above the rank of appointment must be provided, and a four-inch photo must be attached. The above guarantee must prove that the applicant has no circumstances listed in Article 5. The guarantor must sign and seal. Article 7: The examination is divided into written and oral tests. Those who pass the written test are allowed to take the oral test. Article 8: The subjects of the written test are as follows: (1) Chinese; (2) Civil Procedure Law and Criminal Procedure Law, regarding the provisions on document service and execution; (3) Clerk's Job Regulations; (4) Arithmetic (addition, subtraction, multiplication, division, fraction ratio). According to the order, the Three People's Principles are added to the examination. Article 9: The oral test is based on the last three subjects of the previous article. Day of January of the 21st year of the Republic of China, Court President Xu Weiqiu.

Qin Runqing's Mother's Death

Mrs. Yan, the mother of Mr. Qin Runqing, a leader in the silver industry in this port, passed away in her hometown of Cixi on the 9th of this month, at the age of 85. Because the Lunar New Year is approaching, Mr. Qin followed the tradition of burial for peace and wanted to choose a burial place to appease the spirit. He has decided to hold a memorial service on the 20th of this month and a funeral on the 21st at his residence in Dajiao Alley in Cixi City. The funeral procession will be held on the 22nd. However, Mr. Qin followed his mother's last words and did not dare to disturb relatives and friends. Therefore, he did not send obituaries to relatives and friends in Shanghai, Cixi, and other places. However, many of Mr. Qin's acquaintances have recently traveled to Ningbo by boat and then to Cixi to offer their condolences.

Meeting of Tenants in Shenyu Lane

All the tenants of Shenyu Lane on Huacheng Road in the Jiang Concession held a general meeting at the Nanyangqiao Chamber of Commerce at approximately 5:00 PM the other day. More than 50 people attended. Li Chengzhang was publicly elected as chairman and reported on the unsuccessful peaceful negotiations with the landlord. Then, the discussion turned to countermeasures. The following resolutions were made: (1) Deny the one-month rent compensation for losses. (2) In order to seek perfection, the tenants should compensate for at least three months of losses, or reduce the rent by 10% per month. (3) If the goal is not achieved, all tenants should prepare to deposit the rent in the bank to avoid being sued for rent arrears. (4) All negotiation expenses will be paid by all tenants at a rate of $40 per room. (5) The details of the landlord's lack of sincerity in reconciliation will be reported to the competent authorities and assistance will be sought from all sectors. (6) The expenses will be kept by three committee members who will be responsible for collection. (7) If any tenant violates the public agreement or does not comply with the resolutions, they will be responsible for any losses incurred. All of the above proposals were passed. Then, the date for depositing the rent in the bank and collecting the expenses was decided. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

Letter

Chinese Students Do Not Apply to the Spirit of "The Last Lesson" Zhou Jingxiang

But do not engage in reckless actions that are exploited by others.

National salvation must come from practical material aspects.

Today, reading Mr. Wang Maoxun's three answers, especially regarding the question of students, using the history of the French "The Last Lesson" as an example, he believes that Chinese students should also adopt this attitude and does not agree with strike actions. After reading it, I feel that there are different opinions.

Originally, the calm attitude of French students is indeed worthy of our admiration. Of course, it would be best if we in China could also have these examples. However, in reality, even if our students can do it, the environment in our country simply won't work. Just look at the current national crisis. Where have the authorities shown any active expression? The country raises millions of soldiers, but when foreign enemies invade, they only know how to retreat without resistance. Within a day, thousands of miles of land are lost, creating a strange story unheard of in the world. At this time of national demise, fortunately, we have passionate young students who sacrifice their precious study time, fearlessly and tirelessly, to shout out and awaken our compatriots. China has a large population, but many are numb and apathetic. Without such shouting, many sleeping lions cannot be awakened. This time, our people have shown a strong sense of national spirit. Unfortunately, the authorities are brave in internal strife but cowardly against external enemies, betraying the patriotic heart of the people. But these spirits will not diminish, and the unity of these spirits is greatly due to the students. Perhaps some people say that now that the noise is over and the fuss is over, what is the reality? The land is still lost, the humiliation is still humiliation, the authorities are still not awake, and the internal strife is still intense. Students, they have only sacrificed their studies. This is indeed reasonable, but on the other hand, if there had been no enthusiastic student movement this time, the national spirit of China would have been even more dead. Don't even mention foreigners occupying the three northeastern provinces; even when they reach Tianjin, many people are still numb. In China's environment and under China's authorities, we can only recognize the young students. We urgently need young students to stand up and shout, and even more need students to have active movements. "The Last Lesson" cannot exist in China. France has responsible troops and a responsible government. They will not make the students anxious, nor will they make the students panic. Therefore, even though the Prussian army is sounding the horn, they are still studying. Even though the front line is fighting, they are still studying. What about China? Don't even mention stopping. Our blood is hot and boiling. We cannot be so calm and sit idly by as our country is broken and the map changes color! My meaning is that French students have the French environment, and Chinese students must not imitate this calm spirit of "The Last Lesson." However, meaningless, reckless actions that are exploited by others should be carefully noted. At the same time, we should work hard in science and save the country from a practical material perspective. (Ding)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Friday, January 15, 1932, No Additional Charge Small Forum

Seeking Knowledge to Save the Country · Filth

X Can striking really save the country?

Yesterday at a friend's place, I saw a notice that XX

University sent to the students' families. I have already forgotten the wording of the letter. I still remember the general meaning of the letter:

"If students want to engage in patriotic movements, please do not come to the school to study. If you come to the school to study, you are not allowed to engage in patriotic movements anymore."

At that time, when I saw this letter, I felt greatly unfair for the students. Is it that once they study, they are not allowed to be patriotic? Is it that once they study, they are taught to be docile slaves?

Later, I thought about it and there was some reason:

Is the patriotic movement the only career that students can do? Can't you engage in patriotic movements if you are not a student? If you can engage in patriotic movements even if you are not a student, then why must students engage in patriotic careers?

Now that the country is in crisis, students should quickly abandon their books and thoroughly engage in the cause of the patriotic movement. When the lost territory in the Northeast is completely recovered and Japanese imperialism is overthrown, it will not be too late to go back to school to study.

Furthermore, the title of "student" cannot be casually added. It comes from the huge tuition fees sacrificed by fathers and brothers. Now, sacrificing huge tuition fees and not going to school, but specializing in patriotic movements, is not a concern for wealthy and affluent families. I am afraid that it is not easy for ordinary middle and lower-class families to come up with such large tuition fees, is it? If the country is loved, what about the family?

Furthermore, the will of the students in each school, or the students in one school, may not be completely consistent. Some take patriotism as a prerequisite, and some must take studying as a prerequisite. Now, because students who advocate patriotism as a prerequisite go to engage in patriotic movements, the time, economy, and studies of students who advocate studying as a prerequisite are all sacrificed, which is not justifiable in terms of emotion and reason.

To be more thorough, the families of a few wealthy students do not care about these small tuition fees. They may as well allocate these tuition fees to patriotic movement expenses, or to earthquake relief funds after the great flood in the country last year, when mourners are still everywhere. It can also make the general hunger people grateful and tearful. Or, it may as well take these tuition fees to the Bund to skim water slices and watch the water flowers. It is not impossible. Why must it be sent from the "school store"?

Some say that students' patriotic movements have a background. Some say that students' patriotic movements have other reasons. There is no need to discuss these gossips. Now what I want to ask:

"What is a school? What do students actually learn in school?"

Do students want to engage in patriotic movements? Go ahead and do it, go ahead and do it thoroughly, but there is no need to waste useless tuition fees. Do students want to study? Go ahead and study, go ahead and work hard to study, and then go ahead and do patriotic careers after you have finished studying.

During the May Fourth Movement, Mr. Cai Yuanpei had two sentences: Love the country without forgetting to study, study without forgetting to save the country. Ah! These are really deceiving words.

Blows everyone to open their mouths and laugh,

The northeast wind blows tightly,

Screams to Jiangnan, everything is sad,

Blows the rural farmers wringing ropes, their palms about to split,

Blows the factory workers packing and shedding tears,

Blows the servant girls soaking in water, tears accompanying,

Blows the apprentices' heads shrinking,

Blows the watermen's temples withered,

Blows the poor children crying sadly,

Blows the beggars dead in piles Popular Literature and Art

Popular Science

Flying Fire Zhou Ruiquan

Take a thin glass tube with an inner diameter of two-sixteenths of an inch and a length of about two inches. First, seal one end of the tube with candle oil (sealing wax is also acceptable). With the other end of the tube facing upwards, fill it with sulfuric acid (i.e., strong sulfuric acid s2So4). Be careful not to spill it on your skin to avoid corrosion. Filling method: Use small pliers to hold the tube, and use a small piece of wrapping paper to roll a small funnel (large at the top and pointed at the bottom, leaving a tiny hole at the tip) on the mouth of the tube (do not block the mouth of the tube when inserting the funnel, so that air can escape). Then, drip the sulfuric acid drop by drop onto the funnel in order to fill it. After filling, seal the mouth of the tube with wax oil (both ends of the tube must be sealed tightly to prevent sulfuric acid from leaking).

Put a spoonful of potassium chlorate (kclo3) and a spoonful of sugar together and mix them together. Use a thin sheet of paper six inches long and three inches wide (feet) to spread the mixture on one end of the paper (spread two inches long and three inches wide). Then, cover the entire tube with the glass tube that has been filled with sulfuric acid, and tightly roll it into a cylinder. Tighten the remaining paper at both ends to prevent the mixture from leaking. Then, place it on the ground: Use a small hammer to break it at one end so that the sulfuric acid flows out. It will immediately make a crackling sound and start to burn, emitting green-white light.

Sulfuric acid encounters the mixture of potassium chlorate and sugar, which generates extremely high heat and releases a large amount of oxygen, burning the paper. Not only that, its flame is so fierce that the small glass tube will be completely vaporized.

Street Sociology

Various Ways of Life (3) Xingzi

It was on a summer evening last year, I was walking with two or three friends barefoot on the road next to the French Park to enjoy the cool air. It was already midnight, and pairs of young men and women were being spewed out of the park’s mouth with tired expressions on their faces. The women were all like tame cats, gently embraced under the arms of the men. A breeze swept across every delicate white face, and everyone wore an uncontainable rosy smile. Amidst the group that was letting out soft smiles and sweet whispers, there was a serious groan, which was truly a disturbing sight. I don’t know what kind of psychology made me unable to stop and take a look.

The matter was like this: a man close to fifty was carrying an old woman close to seventy on his back. For every step he took, the man let out a labored gasp, and the old woman let out a low groan. The light shone on their faces, which were simply frighteningly pale. I asked the man, "Why are you carrying such an old person on the road at this late hour?"

So he put down the old woman on his back, his eyes filled with pleading tears, and said haltingly in Hankou dialect: "My original residence is in Hubei. She is my old mother. I originally opened an umbrella shop at Lao Ximen. Unfortunately, there was a fire the night before, and everything was burned. Now there is no place to live. I want to go back to Hankou, but I don't have travel expenses. We haven't eaten for two days. Alas, I am not enough to be pitied, only my old mother is suffering!"

"Do you smoke opium?" I asked him again with suspicion and disbelief.

"Where did you hear that? Sir, I am a well-behaved merchant!"

Suddenly, a man wearing short clothes walked out from the side. He said to himself, "That's true. The fire at the XX umbrella shop in Lao Ximen was something I saw with my own eyes the day before yesterday. It was a really tragic fire."

The words of this man in short clothes dispelled all my doubts and made me feel great sympathy and pity for the unfortunate victim, especially for the dying old woman. I immediately ran back to my residence and brought all my money to him. Still feeling that it was not enough, I borrowed some more from friends to make up the number. Finally, I called a rickshaw for him and told him to temporarily find a small hotel to stay overnight that night and then find a way to return to Hankou.

X X X

Ten days later, my friend Mr. W encountered the same thing on his road, and it was still the same man and still the same old woman. Southeast Northwest

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (9) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong

X First Land Management Regulations

In 1845, Gong Mu Jiu, the Daotai of Songjiang and Taicang, and the British Consul Balfour negotiated and formulated the Land Regulations for the Concessions. These regulations had a significant impact on the subsequent management laws of the international society in the Concessions.

The scope of the Concessions was redefined, and the western boundary was expanded to Changbang, which is now Fujian Road. Foreigners in the Concessions were not allowed to hire police officers, but they could hire bodyguards with the permission of the government. Chinese people were prohibited from living in the Concessions. Furthermore, Chinese people in the Concessions were prohibited from renting houses to Chinese people and were not allowed to renovate houses for rent to Chinese merchants. These Land Regulations completely excluded the influence of Chinese people in the Concessions, and the Chinese people could not set foot in their own country and were subjected to foreign control.

All landlords and major property owners in the Concessions were responsible for maintaining the Concessions and began to collect house donations to cover the costs of all public undertakings in the Concessions. A Roads and Jetties Committee was organized by merchants within the Concessions designated by the British Consul (whether the original Chinese translation was the Roads and Jetties Committee is still to be investigated). They were responsible for collecting taxes, and all tax expenditures were managed by all the local people and landlords. Except for the British, all other foreigners had to abide by these Land Regulations. Therefore, these regulations could only be modified with the consent of Chinese officials and the British Consul.

Within the Concessions, four major roads had been completed. These four roads are now Hankou Road, Jiujiang Road, Nanjing Road, and Beijing Road. These four roads are all east-west parallel lines and are still the most prosperous central areas in the Public Concession. Jiujiang Road is the widest, at twenty-five feet, and the other three roads are each twenty feet wide.

X Establishment of the French Concession

After the establishment of the British Concession in Shanghai, the United States and France sent people to Guangzhou to request the establishment of new concessions. With the permission of the Guangdong Governor Qi Ying, the first French Consul in Shanghai, M. Montigny, agreed with the Daotai of Songjiang and Taicang, Mr. Lin, on April 6, 1849, to establish the French Concession. It extended south to the Chenghuang River (now MinGuo Road), east to the Huangpu River, west to Guandi Temple River, and north to Yangjingbang.

After the establishment of the French Concession, French imperialists, like British imperialists, excluded all other labor from setting foot in the Concession. Therefore, Chinese officials and officials of any other country could not interfere in matters within the French Concession.

Manuscript Solicitation Regulations for the Local Supplement

㈠ Various essays on literary, artistic, and social topics, such as (1) Poems and short essays related to current events (2) Essays on social issues, whether for improvement, criticism, or satire

㈠ In addition to the above two categories, this publication welcomes any other highly interesting and valuable essays. However, contributors should note that all essays should preferably be related to Shanghai facts.

㈠ Manuscript fees are divided into three grades: A, B, and C. Grade A is four yuan per thousand words, Grade B is three yuan, and Grade C is two yuan. Special manuscripts may be paid separately.
